After eating a full meal for dinner, they set up a sentry post. When a ship passed Hongni Weir Town in the north, it was robbed of four hundred yuan.

Local News

Municipal Chamber of Commerce Telegraphs Request for Thorough Abolition of Likin 82

Prohibiting Provinces and Regions from Delaying Under Various Pretexts

Strictly Forbidding the Establishment of Various Items Under Likin

The Municipal Chamber of Commerce sent a telegram to the Ministry of Finance in Nanjing yesterday, stating, "We have received Your Ministry's general telegram that all likin and similar transit taxes should be permanently abolished by December 31st of this year. Decades of sick merchants and corrupt policies have been removed in one day. The chronic disease has recovered, and there is hope. It fully demonstrates the government's adherence to the legacy of the late Premier, which is clear and decisive. We are deeply impressed. We are concerned that provinces may use the excuse of financial difficulties to delay the matter or create various items to continue their demands. This would undermine the success of the project. We have read the general telegram, which also earnestly warns us about this. The association believes that likin has long been included in national taxes, and land taxes are entirely local. Therefore, this abolition of likin, even if there is a loss, falls within the scope of national taxes. Provinces and regions must not use the excuse of no compensation. Moreover, there is a business tax that can be used to supplement it. They must not be allowed to undermine the overall plan and burden the government's new policy. We should resolutely uphold: (1) Do not allow provinces and regions to delay under various pretexts. (2) Strictly prohibit the establishment of various items other than likin. The two items of special consumption tax and business tax that are currently under discussion have outlines for tax items and tax rates that were formulated during the likin abolition meeting. They must be strictly implemented to avoid abuses. Recently, the proposed tax rate for the business tax in Jiangsu Province has been increased tenfold compared to the original outline. The unified tax on yarn factories has been increased to two or four or five times the current rate. This means that one abuse has not been removed, and another abuse has arisen. Merchants who are eagerly awaiting governance will be disappointed. We hope that you will pay close attention to this matter. The third item of the general outline of special consumption tax, which states that the authorities must consult the opinions of commercial organizations, and the fifth item of the business tax outline, which states that a business tax review committee should be jointly established by officials and merchants, must be implemented one by one to ensure that merchants have the opportunity to express their opinions and avoid major mistakes. Even if there are no means of remedy after exhausting appeals, we offer our humble opinions and hope that you will consider them. Shanghai Municipal Chamber of Commerce."

All Circles in this City Are Working Hard to Promote the National Calendar 83

Actively Preparing to Celebrate the New Year

Since the Shanghai Special City Party Department, together with various agencies and groups, organized the Shanghai All Circles Celebration of the National Calendar New Year Preparatory Committee, it has been actively proceeding. The heads of various departments go to the third floor of the Municipal Party Department every day to work. The recent preparations of the committee and the preparations of various districts and groups are recorded on the right:

Special Lecture - The Shanghai All Circles Celebration of the National Calendar New Year Preparatory Committee, in order to actively promote the national calendar, has scheduled to hold a lecture meeting to promote the national calendar for three consecutive days starting tomorrow (28th) on the third floor of the Municipal Party Department. Cai Yuanpei (28th), Yang Xingfo (29th), Wang Jingqi (30th) and other three people have been invited to attend the meeting every day from 2:00 PM to 4:00 PM to give lectures. All agencies and groups in the city must send representatives to attend the lectures on time every day. The number of representatives should be at least four from the district party department, at least two from the district branch, and at least two from each group every day.

Enthusiastic Payment - The fees recognized by various agencies and groups are collected by the preparatory committee sending personnel to various places. Most of them have been paid. Although the total amount of funds this time is not as large as during the National Day commemoration, the responsible personnel of each department are handling everything in the most economical way. Therefore, the shortage is very small.

Screening Films - The preparatory committee's entertainment department initially proposed to issue half-price tickets to various circles. All cinemas in the city would sell tickets at half price upon presentation of the tickets. Later, it was felt that this method was very troublesome. Therefore, the Carlton, Da Guangming, Nanjing (Central City), Southeast, Penglai, Gonghe (South City), Odeon, Guomin, and Shijie (Zhabei) cinemas in the city were requested to screen a film at 10:00 AM on New Year's Day in the 20th year of the Republic of China. The tickets will be printed and distributed to various circles by the preparatory committee. It is heard that the preparatory committee has sent personnel to negotiate separately and has sent a letter to the publicity department of the Municipal Party Department, ordering all cinemas to comply.

Performing Peking Opera - The Zhabei Xin Gengxin stage will perform Peking Opera starting at 1:00 PM on New Year's Day. At that time, the red carpet, the clear singing and graceful dance, and the New Year atmosphere will be even more joyful.

Distributing Free Tickets - The preparatory committee will print 1,000 tickets each for the Great World, Small World, and Bansong Garden and distribute them to various circles to celebrate the grand event.

Central District of Shanghai to Begin Construction in Spring 84

Estimated Construction Cost of 500,000 Yuan

Building New-Style Streets and People's Gardens

Issuing 10 Million Yuan in Public Bonds to Develop the Wusong Commercial Port

The Shanghai Municipal Government plans to build a new Shanghai, originally planning to divide Pudong into eight districts and Pumian into thirty-two districts, totaling forty districts, and to set up a political center area. According to Guo, Secretary of the Municipal Government, the political center area of Yin Xing has been decided to start construction in the spring, with a total fixed cost of 500,000 yuan. In addition to building the Municipal Government and the eight bureaus of Public Security, Public Works, Finance, Land, Education, Social Affairs, and Health, it is also necessary to build two people's gardens. All streets and roads are new-style. Public toilets, electricity, telephones, and other items are also extremely new and complete. The entire plan for New Shanghai was originally scheduled to be completed in ten years, and the construction of the Yin Xing political center area is scheduled to be completed in three years. The main roads are already under construction. The entire design of the new Shanghai city is currently being solicited from all walks of life. Once adopted, it will be rewarded. It is also necessary to develop a commercial port in Wusong. It is planned to issue 10 million yuan in public bonds to finance this project.

Prosperous Yangtze River Shipping of China Merchants Steam Navigation Company 85

It Has Leapt to the Top of the Six Companies

After the military Yangtze River ships were returned, Li Zhonggong, General Manager of the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company, discussed with Shen Zhongyi, head of the business department, and others, and first actively reorganized the Yangtze River route. They dispatched regular ships, added tugs and barges, opened new lines, and handled joint transportation. They also took over the Wuxue lighter and recovered the lost shipping rights. In the past two months, they have been vigorously advancing separately, and the Yangtze River route has achieved results. The Jianglun business of the company, which used to be below Taigu, Yihuo, and Riqing, has now suddenly leapt to the first place among the six companies. The general information heard is recorded as follows:

Pinghan Joint Transportation - Pinghan Road freight transportation has been suspended for more than three years. It was not until November that the entire line was opened due to the end of the military affairs. The goods transported from the Pinghan line to Hankou and then transferred to Shanghai and other places are 1,500 to 2,000 tons per day. Among them, those transported to Shanghai, except for those going to the East Yang transported by Riqing, and those loaded to Shanghai's local street, have been agreed upon by Li Yunliang, Director of the Han Branch of the company, and the Pinghan Railway Bureau. The contract for the joint transportation of vehicles has been signed. All goods transferred from Pinghan Road to Shanghai will be given priority transportation rights by China Merchants Steam Navigation Company. It has already been implemented. Therefore, the company's downstream cargo has greatly increased compared to before.

Adding Ships to Changsha - The Hunan route has been expanded to six times a month since China Merchants Steam Navigation Company resumed operations this year. Recently, due to the export of Xiang rice, it has been agreed that the Xiang province will reduce the export rice donation by 1.5 yuan, and the Wuhan transit fee of 1 yuan will also be exempted. As a result, Hunan rice has begun to be loaded for export. The company has contacted Xiang rice merchants to carry the goods. In order to make up for the insufficient two shipments, it was decided to add another ship. Li Yunliang came to Shanghai this time to discuss the addition of ships and expansion matters with General Manager Li, which has been approved and will be implemented next month.

Prosperous Business - According to the company's survey, there are more than 500,000 tons of miscellaneous grains, cotton, and tobacco stored in Zhengzhou and Xinyang, and most of them need to be transferred to Shanghai for export to various ports. In these two months, the Jianglun business of the company has greatly improved both upstream and downstream. On average, each ship carries about 8,000 pieces of upstream cargo and about 6,000 pieces of downstream cargo. Riqing averages about 6,000 pieces upstream and downstream, Yihuo about 5,000, and Taigu the least, only about 4,000 pieces. Among the six companies, China Merchants Steam Navigation Company has leapt to the first place. Riqing transports slightly more yarn and cloth upstream, and miscellaneous grains are transported downstream to the East Ocean. It occupies the second place.

Navigation Interrupted in Western Hunan - Hunan is an important port for Jianglun business. Although ships can travel on various roads in central Hunan, western Hunan has not been able to open to navigation due to the unrest of the bandits. Tung oil, which is a major item among the downstream goods, is sold especially to the United States. The situation this year is very different. The waterway is blocked, and the United States is already planting tung trees. Therefore, the transportation of Hunan tung oil to the United States has plummeted.

Request to Reduce Water Fees - After the six companies in this port increased the Yangtze River shallow water fee, the Nanzun Railway Transportation Office sent a telegram to the Chinese shipping companies in this port, requesting that the increased water fees of 10% to 50% for upstream and downstream cargo be canceled immediately and the original price be restored. It generally said that the Nanzun transportation has just opened, and there are many goods waiting to be loaded. Foreign shipping companies are increasing the water fees by high-pressure means, and our Chinese shipping companies should not also follow suit and increase the fees to benefit commercial transportation. Sanbei China Merchants Steam Navigation Company, etc., believe that this matter concerns the unified management of the six companies and cannot be uniquely different. Therefore, they did not agree to stop the increase and replied to the Nanzun Railway Transportation Office.

New Locomotives for the Beijing-Shanghai Railway 86

Inviting the Press for a Test Ride

Departed Suzhou at 5:25 AM Yesterday

Journey Time: 2 Hours and 3 Minutes

The Beijing-Shanghai Railway Bureau recently ordered eight Pacific-type locomotives from the British North British Locomotive Company. Upon arrival in Shanghai, the Wusong Machine Factory expedited their assembly. Four locomotives, numbered C53, 54, 55, and 56, have been completed, with the remaining four still being assembled. Yesterday morning at 5:25 AM, the Bureau specifically conducted a test run of the new locomotive (53) between Shanghai and Suzhou, inviting members of the press to ride along. The scheduled arrival time in Suzhou was one hour and fifteen minutes. However, due to the cautious operation of the new locomotive, the journey ultimately took two hours and three minutes. Although there was a sixteen-minute stopover en route, the actual speed only exceeded the express train speed by about ten minutes.

Besides eighteen reporters from various newspapers, the passengers included Mr. White from the Sino-British Company, Chief Engineer Dasifu, Deputy Director Zheng Baozhao of the Traffic Department, Director Fen Ci of the Locomotive Department, Deputy Director Wang Chengzhu, Chief Section Leader Chen Xinghan of the two-route station, Chief Section Leader Fang Bolin of the Beijing-Shanghai Railway, Electrical Inspector Ma Zhishan, and Clerk Lu Dingbei. The test train consisted of one fourth-class carriage, two third-class carriages, one baggage car, and two parlor cars, PC No. 13 and No. 14. The press corps rode in parlor car No. 13, with Deputy Director Zheng Baozhao and Mr. Ma Zhishan accompanying them, providing meticulous reports on everything.

The train departed from the North Station at 5:25 AM yesterday. The sky was still dark. At 5:55 AM, it arrived at Nanxiang Station and departed again at 6:00 AM. The sky gradually brightened, and the speed increased. The Railway Bureau specially prepared breakfast for the guests. At 6:13 AM, the train passed Anting Station. At 6:30 AM, it passed Lujiabang Station. At 6:40 AM, it passed Kunshan Station. At 7:05 AM, it passed Yiting Station. At 7:20 AM, it passed Waikuatang Station. At 7:28 AM, it arrived at Suzhou Main Station. After the passengers disembarked, Mr. Lu Dingbei took a group photo of everyone in front of the new locomotive to commemorate the occasion. The original train remained in Suzhou for several hours, finally departing for Shanghai at 11:10 AM.

Vice-Director of Transportation Zheng Baozhao and Newspaper Reporters take a photo next to the new locomotive when it arrived at Suzhou station (Photographed by Ye Changlie)

According to Deputy Director Zheng Baozhao, the departure time was 5:25 AM, and the arrival time at Suzhou Station was 7:28 AM. Since it was a test run, the train had to be inspected at each station, and oil was added to prevent overheating. The total stopover time at various stations was sixteen minutes, so the actual speed was one hour and forty-seven minutes. The usual speed of the express train is two hours and ten minutes, while that of the slow regional train is two hours and thirty minutes. If the train runs for a slightly longer period of time, the components will become smoother, and the time spent adding oil will be reduced, resulting in a significant increase in speed.

According to Deputy Director Wang Chengzhu of the Locomotive Department, the new locomotive generates steam easily and has a strong pulling force. While the old locomotive could only pull a load of 17,000 pounds, the new one can pull 28,000 pounds. It is equipped with a device that adds water to the hot steam, eliminating the need to directly add cold water to the boiler. It can also use the exhaust steam from the chimney to boil water, which is then fed into the steam boiler, further saving coal. It is said that the railways in Korea and South Manchuria are also using this Pacific-type locomotive. The entire new locomotive is one-third longer than the old locomotive, and the boiler and steam shaft are larger than those of the old locomotive, while the driving wheels are slightly smaller. The locomotive, including the coal car and water car, weighs a total of 156 tons, and it can pull 28,000 pounds. It is worth 8,400 gold pounds, and with the addition of shipping costs and tariffs, it costs a total of 9,000 pounds, which is approximately 200,000 Chinese dollars.

The Beijing-Shanghai Railway Bureau has scheduled the official inauguration ceremony for the new locomotive to be held on the 30th of this month. The train will depart from Shanghai North Station at 10:30 AM on that day, heading directly to Kunshan. At that time, representatives from various agencies and organizations will be invited to ride along. Free test ride tickets will be distributed to various sectors today and tomorrow.

Compensation Funds for the New Da Ming Incident Are Postponed 93

The Japanese Ambassador Replied with the Reasons

Regarding the issue of compensation for the bereaved families of passengers who died in the New Da Ming ship sinking, which was caused by the Japanese ship Atsuta Maru, the Social Affairs Bureau, in conjunction with the Shipping Association, the Seamen's Industrial Union, and the Datong Company, negotiated with the Japanese side. The Japanese trading company Sato & Co. initially only agreed to pay 25,000 yen in compensation. The Social Affairs Bureau and other organizations signed a settlement agreement with the trading company regarding the compensation.

However, the Japanese side has delayed the payment for more than two years, and it has not yet been paid. The families of the victims in Shanghai have spent a considerable amount on waiting for the compensation and on food and lodging expenses. Recently, with the arrival of winter, their living conditions have become even more difficult. They have repeatedly requested the Social Affairs Bureau, the Shipping Association, and other agencies to negotiate for the early receipt of the funds to maintain their livelihoods. Last month, the Ministry of Foreign Affairs again urged the Japanese Legation in China to expedite the payment. Yesterday, a reply was finally received from the Japanese Legation, stating that the compensation could not be paid immediately and would still have to be delayed. The original letter is as follows: "Regarding the collision between the ship No. 2 Atsuta Maru, owned by Japanese trading company Sato & Co., and the ship New Da Ming, owned by your country's Datong Shipping Company, your Ministry's letter of November 4 stated that Sato & Co. had admitted to paying 25,000 yen to the crew and passengers who died in the New Da Ming incident, but the funds had not yet been paid. Please urge the Japanese Consul in Shanghai to order the trading company to pay the funds immediately. This has been forwarded to the Consul General, who has been instructed to take measures to expedite the payment. The settlement agreement regarding this case, which was signed between your country's Datong Shipping Company and Sato & Co., was mediated by the Japanese Consul General to ensure its fulfillment. Furthermore, Sato & Co. is also sincerely raising funds. However, due to the impact of unfavorable market conditions, it has been unable to raise sufficient funds as scheduled. Therefore, the fulfillment of the agreement has been inevitably delayed. Please understand the above-mentioned circumstances and convey them to the Shanghai Municipal Government. The Municipal Government has already notified the Shipping Association and the Seamen's Union to convey the information to the families of the victims."

Letter from the Taxpayers' Association to the Municipal Council 94

Serious Kidnapping Cases Occur Frequently

Loss of Confidence in Guaranteeing Security

Yesterday, the Chinese Ratepayers' Association sent a letter to the Municipal Council, stating: "Since serious kidnapping cases have been occurring frequently in recent years, this Association believes that it is necessary to suppress them vigorously. We have repeatedly written to your Council urging strict prevention and also submitted six suggestions for preventing kidnapping in our letter of June 9 this year. Your Council only sent a letter inviting us to recommend representatives to discuss the matter. This has been delayed until now, with no results. Although your Council's letter No. 42689 of October 29 last year indicated methods for preventing bandits, it seems that your Council is not paying attention to suppression work. Speaking of actively proceeding, in reality, there is no credibility. In the past week, there have been as many as four kidnapping cases reported in the newspapers alone, and it is difficult to say that there are none that have not been discovered. There have even been many deaths and injuries. With a huge defense expenditure of more than 4.7 million, the result is like this, which proves that the Municipal Council's ability to maintain security has a significant question and the safety of taxpayers' lives and property has been lost. It is a fact that cannot be concealed. We do not know whether your Council has the ability to maintain security. Taxpayers will never want millions of residents' taxes to be used in places that cannot guarantee safety. We hope you will investigate and reply to this letter."

Executive Yuan Order on Compliance with Trade Regulations 95

Trade Regulations Set by All Trades in the City

Must Be Submitted to the Social Affairs Bureau for Review

Regarding the case where various trades requested the Social Affairs Bureau to require all trades not affiliated with associations to comply with trade regulations, the Bureau repeatedly submitted a request to the Municipal Government, which was then forwarded to the Executive Yuan for approval. Director Pan also raised the issue at the National Industrial and Commercial Conference. It was resolved that the Ministry of Industry and Commerce should adopt and implement the measure. It was previously reported that the Municipal Government has received Executive Yuan Order No. 4476, and this case has been reported back to the Ministry. According to the Shanghai Municipal Social Affairs Bureau, (1) the industry regulations drafted by various trades must be submitted to the local administrative authorities in charge of industry and commerce for approval and record-keeping; (2) once approved and recorded, they will be regarded as the same regulations and must be jointly observed. Anyone who violates them, whether a member or not, may be reported to the authorities for investigation; (3) when industry regulations encounter practical difficulties, the authorities may add or delete them. These three measures, based on the principle of the minority obeying the majority and reviewed by the authorities to prevent abuses, seem feasible. However, since there are no legal provisions requiring mandatory compliance, to ensure that they are universally implemented, the trade regulations set by the trades must be impartial and seek to be permissible by law. The authorities' review standards should be based on whether or not they harm the livelihood of society and the people. If there are situations such as raising prices, restricting production, arbitrarily setting penalties, or involving labor issues, these must be strictly reviewed.

Page 10

Furthermore, if penalties are set, each case must still be submitted for review and decision, and they must not be implemented without authorization, so as to take into account both legal regulations and commercial realities. After reviewing the Ministry's review points, it seems feasible to take into account both commercial realities and legal regulations. It is hereby ordered that the Municipal Government immediately comply with and implement the measures. The Social Affairs Bureau, after receiving the official document, immediately ordered the Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce to inform the various trade associations and to quickly submit all trade regulations, whether or not they have been submitted to the authorities for record-keeping, to the Bureau for review.

Borrowing Property Rent for Levy Must End by the End of the Year 100

Bonds Will Be Issued to Households Starting in January Next Year

Xin Sheng She stated that the Shanghai Municipal Finance Bureau previously borrowed property rent for the levy of treasury bonds and Shanghai municipal public bonds, which was carried out separately by the four tax collection offices of the bureau. The number of households has now been determined, and the amount of money

has been collected in full. It has now been decided to end this practice at the end of the year. Therefore, the Finance Bureau has recently ordered the four tax collection offices to rush to collect from all households that have been missed during the daily collection, and report the amount collected to the Finance Bureau by the end of the year for forwarding to the Municipal Government to complete the procedures. If households delay payment by the end of the year, the collectors will collect the money again from January 2 to 5 of the 20th year. However, the end will be at the end of this year no matter what. The bonds that should be issued are now stored in the bank and are planned to be issued to households starting in January of the 20th year. However, the minimum denomination of these treasury bonds is 10 yuan, and the minimum denomination of the municipal public bonds is 5 yuan. The property rent collected from each household may vary, making it difficult to handle the odd amounts. The method of handling this is still under discussion.

Changes in Markings in the North Channel of Zhangjia Island 103

Jiang Han Customs River Patrol Director Bai Announced: According to the documents, the markings in the North Channel of Zhangjia Island will be changed. Therefore, in addition to submitting the matter to the Jiujiang Customs Superintendent for approval, the changes will be implemented on approximately the 22nd of this month. The details are listed on the left for the information of all ship owners: (1) The Ba Li Jiang Kou lighthouse will be discontinued; (2) The Ba Li Jiang Lower Section lightship will be installed. The lightship will have two red, constantly lit lights hanging directly above it. The lightship is located at South 42.5 degrees West from the Ba Li Jiang Kou lighthouse, with a distance of 23% of a nautical mile; (3) The Ba Li Jiang lighthouse will be lit. The lighthouse will have two constantly lit lights, one red above and one white below, hanging directly above it. Navigation Guide: Upstream vessels should be approximately 15% of a nautical mile away from the right bank of the river and proceed along the bank until the Ba Li Jiang Lower Section lightship is visible at North 48 degrees West, and then turn to pass the lightship with the starboard side of the vessel approximately 5% of a nautical mile away from the lightship. Then, take the road to pass the Ba Li Jiang lighthouse at a distance of approximately 5% of a nautical mile from the shore, and proceed at this distance until the Wang Jia Ba lighthouse is directly next to the vessel, and then turn outward to take the road to pass the Zhangjia Island North Port lightship, with the port side of the vessel approximately 5% of a nautical mile away from the lightship, and then take the road towards the pagoda on the Jiujiang riverbank. Follow this navigation guide. The shallowest draft in the route was 33 feet on the 15th of this month, while the number recorded on the Jiujiang water gauge was 14 feet and 3/10 of a foot. All the degrees listed above are

according to the compass direction. Yangtze River Downstream Notice No. 1712, Office of the River Patrol Director, December 19, Republic of China Year 19.

Establishment of the Foreign Passport Inspection Office Is Postponed 104

The Shanghai Public Security Bureau, after receiving a copy of the "Regulations on the Inspection of Passports of Foreign Nationals Entering China" issued by the Executive Yuan after forwarding it to the Municipal Government, was also limited to establishing an inspection office within four months from the date of issuance of the order to implement the inspection of passports of foreign nationals entering the country by Chinese police officers before they are allowed to land. The order was issued on August 22, and the implementation period was December 22. Director Yuan has repeatedly convened department meetings to make meticulous plans. However, the matter is of great importance. Shanghai is a major commercial port, and the inspection of passports of foreigners entering the country will be more complicated than in other ports. The allocation and qualifications of personnel must have considerable knowledge and international etiquette to be competent. The number of personnel required is also not something that can be handled by just a few people. It is difficult to get them into compliance without considerable training. Other matters related to funding and organization also require budgeting. The original deadline has passed, and the office cannot be established immediately. It is currently being requested that the opening be postponed.

Shanghai County's Second District Dredges the Zhu Jia Bang 105

The Zhu Jia Bang river in the second district (Tangwan) of Shanghai County enters from the west bank of the East Huangpu River. The river is very long and is one of the Huangpu River's tributaries. Thousands of acres of farmland rely on it for irrigation. It also passes through the Tongren Fuyuan Hall's charitable cemetery, where boats stop to load and unload coffins. Recently, due to the settling of sand, it has gradually become clogged. Therefore, the village chiefs of Sizui, Changgang, and other villages reported the matter to District Chief Peng, who forwarded it for approval. Yesterday, Wu, the Director of the County Construction Bureau, specially dispatched Huang, the director of the Highway Department, and Gong, the section chief of the Technical Section, along with surveyors to the countryside to measure and carry out the dredging.

Liu Maochu's Opinions on Prison Improvement 111

Listed in Five Points

Liu Maochu, Chief Prosecutor of the Shanghai District Court, submitted his opinions on prison improvement yesterday, stating that the quality of prisons is related not only to the lives of prisoners but also to the observation of both domestic and foreign parties. Therefore, although prisons in the East and West are extremely strict, treatment and management strive for appropriateness and are worthy of emulation. In recent years, our country has been keenly focused on rectifying prison administration, but progress has been difficult due to financial constraints. He has been ordered to inspect the Jiangsu Second Prison on a monthly basis, and the equipment situation has been reported and reviewed repeatedly. He has long been aware of the situation. He now respectfully presents the improvements that should be made in the prison, along with additional opinions, as follows: (1) The prison was originally planned to hold 800 inmates, but the number of inmates has now increased to double that. The original two workshops have been converted into communal living rooms, each accommodating hundreds of people, all of whom are serving short-term sentences or are military detainees awaiting trial. The overcrowding is not only a risk for the spread of malicious diseases but also defeats the purpose of imprisonment as a punishment. The solution is to quickly expand the prison facilities or, first, transfer military detainees to other locations. Inmates who meet the conditions for parole should be granted parole to encourage them to reform and change their ways, in line with the original intent of reformation and to avoid overcrowding. (2) The prison originally had seven or eight types of workshops, but they have now been converted into prison rooms. Except for the women's prison, the others have been shut down, and instructors are unable to teach due to the excessive number of inmates, leading to perfunctory efforts. Without work, inmates sit idle all day, and their spirits are dull. Without instruction, they are influenced by what they see and hear, and their will deteriorates day by day. Thus, it is difficult for them to become good citizens after their release. Therefore, it is necessary to find ways to restore the original workshops, assign work, and have instructors rotate daily to provide training. In addition to work and training, they should be allowed to freely read beneficial books. This will not only relieve the inmates' boredom but also allow them to improve themselves and become healthier. (3) The prison holds over 1,500 inmates, and the number of deaths this year has reached 150. Although this may be due to the inmates' weak physical condition, hygiene and medicine must also be improved. The prison used to have two Chinese and Western doctors, but the Western doctor has been dismissed, leaving only one Chinese doctor. It is inevitable that one person will be perfunctory in treating the entire prison. In the future, more doctors should be hired to cope with the situation. In addition, the inmates' diet, bathing, and the ventilation and cleaning of the prison rooms must be carefully attended to so that the inmate mortality rate can be reduced. (4) Many of the prison walls are cracked, and the window panes are broken. It will be difficult to block the wind and snow as the weather gets colder, which will not only affect hygiene but also increase the risk of prison breaks. If repairs are not made quickly, the harm will be significant. (5) Among the prisoners, there are quite a few who are detained for opium addiction. This practice should be improved because the purpose of detention is to restrict freedom and reform. If non-violent opium addicts are housed with ordinary criminals, they may not benefit from reformation but may instead be infected with bad habits. They should be detained separately so that they can quit as soon as possible. The above five points are all significant. Are they feasible? It is appropriate to prepare a document and submit it for review. It is said that Shanghai is observed by both domestic and foreign parties. Mr. Liu is further planning to expand the prison facilities. Before a large amount of funds is available, he still advocates first opening a section that is better than foreign facilities to detain foreign prisoners and those banned from leaving the country.

Raffia Bag Cloth Industry: The Raffia Bag Cloth Industry Guild held its first inaugural meeting yesterday at the original address of the Shantang Guild Hall at No. 3 Xiaolujia Lane, Dadongmen. Because many members are illiterate and find it difficult, according to past practice, the election was conducted by prior written ballot at home, which was sealed and submitted to the meeting for voting. Mr. Hu Yu, the representative of the Social Affairs Bureau, believed that this was illegal and that other guilds might follow suit and cause problems. Therefore, the election was reconducted. Explosion at Nanshi Firecracker Workshop Kills and Injures Eleven 113

Rushing to Produce Firecrackers for the New Year

Sudden Explosion While Packing into Wooden Boxes

Collapses Five Houses

Two Dead, Nine Injured

Around 11:00 PM the night before last, an explosion occurred at the Datong Firecracker Workshop at No. 4 Yufuli, Shijian Tou, south of the Scissors Bridge behind the Nanshi Station Road District Court. Due to improper packing, there was a sudden explosion, destroying a total of five houses and killing or injuring more than ten male and female workers. The details are as follows:

Rushing to produce firecrackers day and night: Chen Yishun, nearly forty years old and a native of Yancheng, runs the Datong Firecracker Workshop at No. 4 Yufuli, Shijian Tou, south of the Scissors Bridge behind the Nanshi Station Road District Court. Business is booming. As the Gregorian New Year is approaching, Chen is seizing the opportunity to hire female workers to produce the most popular firecrackers for the New Year, such as "shuaipao" (whip firecrackers) and "qianpao" (coin firecrackers), in preparation for sale during the New Year to earn a profit.

An unexpected disaster in the middle of the night: Around 11:00 PM the night before last, as the workers were working hard, a group of them were preparing to pack the finished goods into wooden boxes for sale. Due to improper sealing of the wooden boxes, all the firecrackers suddenly exploded. With a loud bang, the explosion shook the surrounding area and completely collapsed two houses in the workshop and three neighboring houses, trapping all the workers inside.

Fire trucks to the rescue: After the incident, people nearby heard the alarm. Fortunately, the Station Road Police Station of the Second District Police Department was nearby. Patrol Officer Ma Deshan led many police officers to the scene. They urgently used the telephone to report to the Second District Police Department and the South District Fire Department. Soon, fire trucks from various routes arrived one after another, and they actively dug and rescued the trapped workers.

Investigation of the number of dead and injured: After about an hour of rescue efforts, a total of eleven injured men and women were pulled out. Two of them died due to their severe injuries. The lightly injured included Hu Liansheng (male, 11 years old, Yancheng native), Hu Genxiao (female, 14 years old, Yancheng native), Ji Dashunzi (male, 12 years old, Yancheng native), Ji Xiaoshunzi (male, 10 years old, Yancheng native), Zhang Shoukang (male, 37 years old, Yancheng native), Zhang Tan's wife (60 years old, Huai'an native), and Zhang Xiaobao (female, 17 years old, Huai'an native). The seriously injured included Liu Gao's wife (30 years old, Huai'an native), Chen Xiaosanzi (28 years old, Huai'an native), Hu Xueyu (17 years old, Yancheng native), Gen Rong (12 years old, Yancheng native), Zhang Yeqi (17 years old, Yancheng native), Hu Wang's wife (37 years old, Yancheng native), Zhang Jiang's wife (27 years old, Huai'an native), and Zhang Yuehong (24 years old, Huai'an native). One of the deceased was Dai, the wife of Xu Jiancheng from Yancheng (20 years old, Yancheng native, died at 2:00 AM yesterday morning from severe facial burns). The other was Zhao Song, the four-year-old daughter of neighbor Liu Yongkang (died on the spot from burns to the chest and abdomen).

Court examination of the body yesterday: At the time, the police officers of the Second District Police Department sent the injured to Shanghai Hospital and Xin Puyu Hall for treatment. They also ordered Gu Tiyun, the local bailiff of the Twelfth Ward, to report to the District Court for an examination. Yesterday afternoon, Prosecutor Lei and others arrived at the scene for an examination and ordered the families to collect the bodies. Chen Yishun, the owner of the workshop that caused the accident, has been arrested and handed over to the court for investigation.

Suspicious Youth Arrested and Shot 114

Carrying Two Paper Packages

Full of Reactionary Leaflets

At around 4:00 AM yesterday morning, Chinese Constable No. 354 of the French Concession's Dazimingzhong Police Station, while on duty in front of Cheng Yuan Tobacco Shop at No. 94 Zhubaoshan Road, suddenly noticed a youth looking flustered, seemingly darting out of the shop. Upon seeing the constable, the youth appeared alarmed and ran away. The constable immediately gave chase, eventually catching up with the youth in a small alley on Fuzhou Road in the Public Concession. The youth turned around and started fighting the constable, attempting to escape. In desperation, the constable drew his pistol and fired a shot at the youth's lower body, hitting his leg. The youth fell to the ground and was immediately taken to the Public Concession police station. After a brief interrogation by the chief of police, the constable was instructed to take the youth to the Dazimingzhong Police Station, and then transferred to the Lujiawan General Police Station. The two paper packages left behind by the youth were examined and found to contain reactionary leaflets. The youth only confessed to being a thief. Further investigation will be conducted after he recovers from his injuries.

American Silver Ingots Arrive in China 115

Contributing to the Decline in Silver Prices

According to the World News Agency, starting in early December, Japanese mail ships and others began shipping large quantities of silver ingots from the United States to China. Japanese mail ships alone have shipped four or five times, each time carrying about 300,000 ounces of silver ingots (approximately 100,000 yuan). In addition, ships such as the Da Lai also carry considerable silver ingots each time. This export of American silver is the result of the disposal of silver ingots from the American private silver agreement. The decline in silver prices is also one of the reasons.

"Rented Wife" Abandoned Midway 116

Sues for Alimony

Resulting in a Rescheduled Hearing

Zhang Yucheng, a Ningbo native, rented Xie Sanzi, a widow, as a wife, according to Ningbo customs, because his wife was infertile and extremely jealous, making it impossible to take a concubine. He hoped to have a son. However, as soon as Xie became pregnant, Zhang's wife learned of it and led a group of women to beat Xie severely, causing a miscarriage. Xie then sued Zhang and his wife in the Special District Court for assault and battery. The defendant, Zhang Yucheng, hired lawyer Zhan Jifeng to defend him. As a result, the case was dismissed on the grounds that the plaintiff's evidence was insufficient. Xie has now filed a civil lawsuit, claiming that according to the "rented wife" contract, the rental period was three years, and the monthly rent was 15 yuan. Because Zhang abandoned her midway, she is destitute and asks the court to order the defendant to pay alimony. Zhang again hired lawyer Zhan Jifeng to defend him. The case was scheduled for trial yesterday afternoon. Both parties arrived in court as summoned. Lawyer Zhan then requested a rescheduling, and although the opposing party objected, Judge He granted the defendant's request and ordered a postponement for a later hearing.

Unsuccessful Divorce Agreement, Filing for Divorce 117

Shen Cuijuan Not Tolerated by Husband's Family

Has Received No Money for Two and a Half Years

Divorce Agreement at Hotel Fails

Shen Files a Lawsuit Hoping for Divorce

Cai Zilin, a native of Ningbo residing at No. 519 Fuqing Lane, East-West Huade Road, works on a ship. His father used to be a compradore on a Taikoo Company ship. He hired Shen Cuijuan, a woman from Zhenjiang, as his wife. People from Ningbo are deeply superstitious, especially women. After the betrothal gifts were exchanged, Cai's father suddenly went blind. Cai's stepmother, Qiu, blamed the daughter-in-law for having a bad fate. Not long after the marriage, Cai's father lost his job as a compradore, further increasing the stepmother's hatred of the daughter-in-law, calling her a "white tiger star." Later, Zilin had a falling out with his stepmother and moved out with his wife, and their relationship gradually improved. However, it did not last long, and they had disagreements. The summer before last, Zilin left his wife and went to Hanzhong alone, not giving her any money for two and a half years. Shen lived on borrowed money. Around the tenth month of the lunar calendar, Cai's cousin, Hu Zifu, suddenly visited Shen, saying that he had been entrusted by Cai's mother to advise her to divorce. Shen believed that her husband had not supported her for a long time, and having a husband was the same as not having one, so she agreed. They chose a lucky day and went to Room 28 of the Huishan Hotel in Ti Lan Bridge to hold a divorce. They decided to have someone write two copies of a divorce agreement, but Zilin suddenly regretted it and refused to sign, so the divorce agreement could not be realized. However, Shen believed that this matter was not a child's play, and Zilin had venereal disease, so if they lived together again, she would be infected. Therefore, she hired a lawyer to file a lawsuit in the Special District Court, requesting a divorce and ordering the defendant to return the 120 yuan she had borrowed and to pay 600 yuan for 30 months of living expenses that he had abandoned. The court hearing was held yesterday morning. After the plaintiff Shen Cuijuan made her statement, witness Hu Zifu described in detail the process of negotiating the divorce with both parties, saying that the reason for the sudden change of heart was that Shen did not hand over the items that Cai wanted back, so Zilin was unwilling to sign. When questioned, the defendant Cai Zilin denied entrusting Hu to propose a divorce to the plaintiff. Cai's stepmother, Qiu, also appeared in court and stated that she did not ask Hu to mediate, and that this matter was purely caused by Hu's meddling between the two parties. She hired lawyer Fan Gang to defend her. Judge Xu Wenrong instructed both parties to go outside and try to reconcile. The case was adjourned for a later hearing.

When paying donations, they should be sure to receive a boat donation license and a stamped or bureau-sealed receipt to avoid being deceived and suffering losses.

Mr. Xiao Xin'an's Letter to the Overseas Chinese Association 122

Ms. Xiao Xin'an sent a letter yesterday to the Overseas Chinese United Association and the Shanghai Women's Association, saying: "I respectfully acknowledge receipt of your telegram. Xin'an is unfortunate, having met with disaster midway. I am deeply grateful for your righteous support. I recently heard that many of my compatriots in Singapore have been driven out because they tried to assist Xin'an in avenging her humiliation. Fellow passengers on the ship dared not help me, which is why this happened. Relying on strength to bully the weak—where is the justice? Not only has my disgrace not been redressed, but it has also burdened other overseas Chinese. Moved by your kindness and righteousness, I must obey your instructions and come forward. However, I cannot yet determine the date of my departure. Xin'an's elderly mother regards Xin's humiliation as the greatest misfortune for our family and has already fallen ill. If those thugs continue to escalate, Xin will certainly not allow the matter to end there. The reason I have been clinging to life for a few days is for my elderly mother. Soon, I will share my experiences from this trip south, as well as the knowledge that my female compatriots should have for prevention and the responsibilities we should embrace in our careers, with all circles, so that we may avoid repeating my mistakes. I do this to repay the enthusiasm of your support. Then I will end Xin's life with death. Writing this, I am overwhelmed with grief and cannot express all that is in my heart. Because of financial constraints, I was unable to reply by telegram. I hope you will forgive me. Xiao Xin'an bows."

Preliminary Announcement of the Shanghai Branch of the Engineering Society's New Year's Celebration 123

The Shanghai branch of the Chinese Engineering Society customarily holds a New Year's celebration every year. A considerable number of members' family and friends attend. This year's celebration has been decided to be held on January 10 at the New World Restaurant. It is estimated that around 500 to 600 people will attend. In addition to games and other entertainment, there will be gifts available for a raffle to add to the fun and serve as mementos. Various industrial and commercial circles, both Chinese and foreign, plan to use this opportunity for publicity and introductions. The general office of the society has already received many exquisite gifts from various famous manufacturers. It is also reported that the society plans to print advertisements for the gifting manufacturers in the program to enhance promotion.

Indian Girl Killed by Car 124

Gao A'wu Fined Two Hundred Yuan

The seven-year-old daughter of Indian Ah Mai Xing was fatally injured on Yangshupu Road by car number 2092 driven by driver Gao A'wu on the evening of the fifteenth of last month. The police have detained Gao and turned him over to the Special District Court. The court ordered him to be detained while the circumstances of the accident were investigated before further questioning. The Indian, grieving deeply for his daughter, has hired lawyer Fan Gang to file a lawsuit demanding legal punishment and to bring a private suit seeking damages of 10,000 taels of silver. Judge Xiao opened the trial yesterday. According to police lawyer Zhang Tianyin, at the time of the accident, someone witnessed the Indian attempting to cross the road to take a tram. In the middle of the road, one of her leather shoes fell off because it was too big. The Indian girl turned back to pick up the shoe, just as the car was speeding by and could not stop. As a result, the girl was hit by the car. However, this witness is unwilling to testify in court, so this report cannot be trusted. However, according to the vehicle regulations, cars should drive slowly wherever trams pass, but the defendant was still driving fast, which constitutes negligence. He also submitted a map of the accident scene as evidence. The defendant firmly stated that he did not intentionally cause the accident. Judge Xiao reviewed the evidence and ruled that Gao A'wu should be fined 200 yuan. The number of days in custody can be used to offset the fine at a rate of two yuan per day. If imprisonment is substituted, it will be calculated at a rate of two yuan per day. The attached civil suit was transferred to the civil court for trial.

Shi Qiaoxing Tragically Killed Under a Car Shortly After His Wedding 125

Yesterday at around 11:30 AM, the Ruiji Flour Company on Arab Street ordered driver Ren Dezhou to drive truck number 3220, registered with the municipal government, to transport rice to the French Concession. Unexpectedly, while driving on Xinmin Road in Zhabei, an old man and a young man were walking slowly ahead. Ren attempted to turn and pass them, but the car was too large and could not avoid them. The young man was knocked down, and the rear wheels ran over his waist. He fainted on the spot. The old man fell to the ground and cried bitterly. The police on duty arrived and took the injured man to the Pushan Hospital for treatment, but the injuries were too severe, and he died without receiving treatment. The police then detained the driver Ren Dezhou and the old man and took them to the Fourth District Headquarters. According to the old man's statement, his name was Wang Fengtai from Yancheng, and the deceased was named Shi Qiaoxing, who was my nephew-in-law. He had just gotten married recently. Today, we went to visit relatives. Who would have thought that disaster would strike so close at hand and he would be killed by a car? However, the driver did not honk the horn. A strict investigation should be requested. The chief then ordered that they be handed over to the bureau for interrogation and ordered the local leader to report to the court for an autopsy. In the afternoon, Commissioner Lei arrived to conduct an autopsy and confirmed that he had been run over and killed by a car. He ordered the family to prepare a coffin for burial.

Sea Bandits Burn Fishing Boats in Nankan Port 126

The sea bandits outside the Wusongkou digging area, near the towns of Zhen and Tao and Ping, have been causing disturbances again. The night before last, they fired rapid cannons at the seaside as a warning to see if there were any precautions taken on the shore, plunging the villagers, who had just calmed down, into panic again. Yesterday morning at around 4 AM, a large number of bandit boats suddenly arrived at Nankan Port. Without asking any questions, they surrounded more than ten fishing boats, including those of Zhang Shunlai, Ge Yuting, and Xu Qianfa, and set them on fire. Fortunately, the fishermen all lived on the shore and were not harmed. However, fearing the bandits' violence, they all dared not go there and could only sigh in despair at the sea. Therefore, the various ports there have invisibly entered a state of closure.

Gang of River Bandits Apprehended in Jiangbei 127

And Seized a Significant Amount of Arms

Page 12

The Fourth District of the Jiangsu River Police Bureau, acting on a tip that a gang of river bandits from the Jiangbei area, led by Gu Ziheng, was hiding in the Gaochang Temple area of Shanghai, purchased information from the district and dispatched special agent Zhang Zhaoxiang, leading a number of detectives, along with the informant, on a small steamer to Gaochang Temple. There, they joined forces with Gao Hongbao, a police officer from the Gaochang Temple Police Station of the Second District of the Shanghai Municipal Police Bureau, and patrol chief Zou Tieshan. At around 11 PM the night before, they secretly went to the address for investigation. At house number 7, South Lane, Gaochang Temple, they apprehended Gu Ziheng, Li Yaokui, and Wang Da'wu. They also found six wooden-cased pistols. Furthermore, on a small Jianghan-Jiangbei boat on Zhuhu Road by the river, they seized fourteen old rifles. They then returned to house number 7, South Lane, and apprehended Liang Dazhong and Feng Youheng. (Liang and Feng were previously workers in the arsenal but had resigned due to an incident.) They were taken, along with the bandit weapons, to the Gaochang Temple Police Station. Then, the special agent of the Fourth District of the Water Police and others escorted them on a small steamer to the Fourth District of the Water Police for interrogation and prosecution.

Lottery Den Busted in Lan Ni Du 128

Yesterday at 11 AM, a dockworker named Li Xiaoxizi went to the Third District of the Pudong Municipal Police Bureau to report that a secret lottery den with a listening device had been set up in house number 15, Taiping Lane, Houshi Qigan Lane, Lan Ni Du, luring people to gamble, causing great harm to the local people. He requested that they be arrested. District Chief Zhang Mingqin, upon receiving the report, immediately ordered patrol chief Wu Ruixiang to lead police to the address for arrest. They apprehended Chen Yuanmo and Wang Shanqing, seized 58 lottery tickets, gambling funds of three yuan and forty cents in silver, four cents in small silver coins, and eighty copper coins. The witnesses were also taken to the district for interrogation. According to Chen Yuanmo, he was 35 years old, from Yangzhou, and lived at house number 2, Lujia Du. He stated that he worked for Song Deming as a boatman and that he was not the one who did the lottery. Wang Shanqing stated that he was 38 years old, formerly a policeman in the third precinct of the first district, and currently lived in Song Deming's house. He said that Song Deming was writing the lottery tickets, etc. While the district chief was preparing to hand them over, Chen Yuanmo's wife, Li, claimed that Li Xiaoxizi's father, Li Guangtao, was eating red pills, which was also illegal. Harboring a fixed idea to avenge her husband, she brought Guangtao and his smoking paraphernalia to the police station. The district chief considered that Li's accusation against Li's father for eating red pills was made with malice and had solid evidence, so he decided not to send him over. As for Li Xiaoxizi, who did not shy away from resentment and reported the lottery listening device, ridding society of a scourge, his actions were proper and he was commended in person. Chen Yuanmo, Wang Shanqing, Li Guangtao, and others were all sent to the General Bureau for interrogation and investigation.

Cheated After Greedily Buying Half-Price Tickets 130

Shen Changke Suffers at the Hands of a Fellow Villager

Shen Changke, a 20-year-old from Hai'an, who lives outside the Xiaonanmen Qinglong Bridge in the Nanshi area and makes a living pulling rickshaws, urgently needed to return to his hometown due to important matters at home. Yesterday afternoon at around 3 PM, he arrived at the 16th Pier to board a ship. He suddenly met a fellow villager he did not know, named Huo Chengzhang, who was serving as a soldier under the First Division of the National Revolutionary Army. Huo approached him and said, "I am a soldier and can buy you a half-price ticket." Shen, hearing that he could get a bargain, was very pleased. He immediately gave Huo one yuan in silver to buy the ticket. Unexpectedly, Huo left and never returned. Shen waited for a long time without seeing him and realized he had been cheated. He was very upset and immediately rushed ashore, searching everywhere. He found him in a small alley, grabbed him, and reported him to Kong Yubin, the guard officer of the Fourth Station there. He was taken to the First District Headquarters, where he was ordered to be temporarily detained pending investigation and review.

The Zhou Woman Is in Love with Her Paramour 131

Unwilling to Return to Her Husband

Zhang Jinchao, a 32-year-old from Gaoyou, makes a living farming in his hometown. He hired a Zhou woman from the same village as his wife seven years ago through a matchmaker. The Zhou woman, now 27 years old, gradually saw that her husband's family was in dire straits and had no production. She was very frustrated. Zhou's uncle, Liu Wenzhong, a 40-year-old carpenter whose wife had died early, was also looking to remarry. He saw that Zhou was still quite attractive and took the opportunity to seduce her. Zhou was also very pleased, and soon they fell in love. In September two years ago, they fled together to Shanghai under the pretext of working as hired laborers. They lived together on a boat in Dongjiadu, living like husband and wife. Before long, she was secretly pregnant, and her belly gradually grew. In August this year, she gave birth to a daughter. Unexpectedly, good things rarely last. Their secret union was discovered by her husband, Zhang Jinchao, who immediately came to Shanghai a few days ago, staying with relatives in Hongqiao in the western suburbs. After investigating the address in detail, he went to Dongjiadu at around 5 PM yesterday and found Zhou. He forced her to go home, but she refused to comply at all costs, resulting in a major conflict. Lu Rongchang, the guard officer of the 16th Station, saw the commotion and arrived. After learning the details, he took them to the first sub-station of the first district for the director to review and handle.

A Person Using Counterfeit Money in the Penglai Market 132

Yesterday morning at around 11 AM, Chen Hanjiao, who lives at house number 1231, Zhonghua Road, and runs a cigarette paper shop, brought a ten-yuan banknote from a certain bank to buy two yuan worth of medicine at the Wuzhou Pharmacy branch in the market. He wanted to get change, but the female staff members Xie and Zhuang Yongfen noticed that the banknote had different patterns and paper. They secretly asked the neighboring shop to verify it, and it turned out to be counterfeit money. They asked Chen about its origin, realizing that someone was using counterfeit money. They reported it to the police officer Xi Qishan of the Second Sub-station of the Second District, who brought Chen Hanjiao and the counterfeit money to the station for investigation.

Two Ship Accidents Also Recorded 133

The Seventh Factory of Fuxin Flour hired Cao A'tang's dock boat the day before yesterday to load 1,200 bags of flour. It was berthed outside the Hubei steamboat at the Taikoo Company's Pier Number Three in the French Concession. During the night, the Hubei steamboat began to weigh anchor and sail, and Cao's boat was immediately moved to the outside of the Taiyuan steamboat at Pier Number Four to berth. Not long after, the Tongzhou steamboat docked at Pier Number Three. Suddenly, the back propeller opened. The current was very strong, causing Cao's boat to capsize and lose more than 300 bags of flour. Yesterday afternoon at 3 PM, Gao Zhiliang's coal boat, carrying 30 tons of cooked coal, was sailing south from the Lujiazui pier. At that time, the Japanese steamer Longtian Mountain Maru was sailing outward and collided head-on with the coal boat. There was no time to avoid it, causing five sideboards on the right middle side of the coal boat to be damaged. River water flooded in, and it immediately sailed to the river beach, avoiding sinking. It is reported that the losses are as high as a thousand yuan.

The Reward to Police for Opium Case Fines 136

Since our country has been strictly enforcing opium prohibition, there has been a provision in various places to reward senior police officers with a percentage of the fines imposed by the courts in opium cases. This has been implemented for many years and has been very effective. The Shanghai District Court has clearly calculated the fines imposed by the court on the various district police stations of the Municipal Police Bureau from January to October. According to regulations, 50% of the funds will be set aside as rewards, with the court deducting 30% and the remaining 20%, approximately more than 3,000 yuan in silver. The Bureau Chief of the Municipal Police Bureau, Yuan, has sent a member to the court to collect these funds and distribute them to the senior police officers of various districts who have solved opium cases, as ordered. Yesterday, an order was issued to all subordinates to bring the instructions for handing over opium cases to the accounting office for collection and distribution as a reward.

Autopsy of Ding Zhixian, Who Was Assassinated 137

Ding Zhixian, a 26-year-old Ningbo native living at house number 3, Ruyi Street, Nanshi, worked as a detective for Dong Mingde, a detective at the First District Police Bureau in Nanshi. On the evening of the 2nd of this month, at 9:30 PM, Ding was walking in front of house number 17, Yuxing Street, outside the Xiaodongmen in the French Concession when he was suddenly shot by someone with a handgun hidden in their sleeve. Ding was hit in the head, injured, and fell to the ground. The assassin immediately fled. The patrol police arrived and took Ding to the police station and then to Renji Hospital. Due to the severity of his injuries, he died on the previous day. The hospital notified the police station, who sent detectives to transport the body to the Tongren Fuyuan Hall morgue for an autopsy. Yesterday, the Criminal Division of the French Police Station ordered detectives to inform the deceased's mother, Ding Wang, to come to the case. Judge Zhu, an adjudicating official from the French Concession, arrived at the morgue at 2:30 PM to examine the body, sat in the official position, and questioned the victim's family. He ruled that the deceased Ding Zhixian was indeed assassinated before his death. The family was allowed to prepare a coffin for burial themselves. The police were ordered to take photos for records. After the autopsy was completed, the family put the body in a coffin and temporarily stored it in the Bing House of the Siming Guildhall.

Chen Jisheng's Autopsy Confirms He Died of Poisoning 138

Chen Jisheng, a local who worked in a foreign firm, committed suicide by taking poison in the Hongfa Store at house number 111, Mintiniyin Road, in the French Concession. His body was taken to the morgue for an autopsy. The details have been reported in the newspapers. It is now known that Chen opened room number 14 at the store on the 20th and stayed for three nights. Chen paid six jiao and six fen for the room and gave one yuan per day, including tea and wine tips, so the waiter treated him like an honored guest, serving tea and water with extra care. When Chen got up to leave the store on the 23rd, he told the waiter that if he did not come by 10 PM, the room could be sold. However, after 10 PM that night, the waiter did not see Chen arrive and gave room number 14 to another guest. At 11 PM, Chen returned to the store and was given room number 28 on the third floor to sleep in. Unexpectedly, Chen suddenly had a suicidal thought that night and swallowed poison. The next morning, the maid entered the room to empty the chamber pot and saw Chen smoking a cigarette, acting normally. But at noon, the waiter called Chen to get up and knocked on the door, but there was no response. He forced the door open and found that Chen had died. The store owner, Yang Guoliang, reported to the police, who took the body to the Tongren Fuyuan Hall morgue for an autopsy. No family members were found. Yesterday, the Criminal Division of the French Police Station reported to Judge Zhu of the French Concession, who arrived at the morgue and confirmed that the deceased had indeed died by taking poison. He ordered photos to be taken and ordered the Tongren Fuyuan Hall to provide a coffin for burial and to store the body in the altar to wait for family members to claim it.

Weather Report 148

The Xujiahui Observatory issued a weather forecast at 4:30 PM yesterday, stating that the weather in the Yangtze River basin and the Shandong coast will be clear and cold with gradual changes. There is a cyclone in Liaodong. The coast here and the Yangtze River basin will have southeast to southwest winds. The Taiwan Strait will have northeast winds. Also, within the 24 hours before 3:00 PM yesterday, the highest temperature in this city was 55.8 degrees and the lowest was 30.2 degrees. On the same day last year, the highest was 49.5 degrees and the lowest was 44.0 degrees.

Letter

To the esteemed Chief Editor:

I am writing to you because I recently read a news item in your newspaper's local news column titled "Guangdong Woman Run Over and Killed by Car" that slightly deviates from the facts. I am writing to request a correction to conform to the truth. My mother, Du You (not You Du, presumably a mistake when reporting from the Zhabei Fifth District Public Security Bureau), was widowed at a young age and only had one daughter. Her livelihood was precarious, and she made a living by making and selling shoe uppers. On the morning of November 29th of this year, she returned the shoes to Yiyuan Company. After finishing her business, she took a rickshaw home. When she was approaching Baoshan Road, she was pushed over by someone pushing a cart, causing the rickshaw my mother was riding in, along with the rickshaw puller, to overturn. Not only did the cart not stop immediately, it continued to advance aggressively, intending to escape, crushing my mother's left tibia. Fortunately, a passerby surnamed Lu saw what happened and chased back the cart. He immediately called the police, and the cart puller, Wang Er, was taken to the Fifth District, then transferred to the General Bureau, and finally to the Local Court. My mother was first admitted to Zhabei Jisheng Hospital, then to the Blue Cross Qianyi Hospital, and finally to Renji Hospital. The Local Court has summoned people several times, but I am a weak woman, and my mother is in great pain in the hospital and cannot be left for a moment. Therefore, I asked my Liang Kui to represent me at the court hearing and request the cart puller and the cart owner to jointly be responsible for compensating all losses. Unfortunately, my mother passed away in the hospital at 7:00 PM on the 23rd of this month due to her injuries. The Local Court has sent personnel to verify the facts and is waiting to summon for handling. The cart puller is still in custody, and the compensation for losses has not yet been resolved. I am afraid that the rumors are untrue. I have always admired your newspaper for upholding justice. Please publish this letter in the correction column to clarify the truth. I am deeply grateful.

Respectfully awaiting your continued success,

Du Hengying and Liang Kui, 615 Qiujiang Road, Zhabei.
